<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_80fd8ee2-7934-4f38-a1d1-8269fee12489'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer15590440534132459055"><i>Librarian's note: This is an Alternate Cover Edition for ISBN10: 0752876457 ISBN13: 9780752876450.</i><br/><br/>A sinister fire in a Copenhagen bookstore ignites a relentless hunt across four continents. Arson and murder reveal an insidious plot to steal a Bible that once belonged to Charles Darwin, the father of evolutionary theory. And Commander Gray Pierce dives headlong into a myste</span>
  <span id="freeText15590440534132459055" style="display:none"><i>Librarian's note: This is an Alternate Cover Edition for ISBN10: 0752876457 ISBN13: 9780752876450.</i><br /><br />A sinister fire in a Copenhagen bookstore ignites a relentless hunt across four continents. Arson and murder reveal an insidious plot to steal a Bible that once belonged to Charles Darwin, the father of evolutionary theory. And Commander Gray Pierce dives headlong into a mystery that dates back to Nazi Germany . . . and to horrific experiments performed in a now-abandoned laboratory buried in a hollowed-out mountain in Poland.<p>A continent away, madness ravages a remote monastery high in Nepal, as Buddhist monks turn to cannibalism and torture. Lisa Cummings, a young American doctor investigating the atrocity, is suddenly a target of a brutal assassin working for clandestine forces that want the affair buried at any cost. Lisa's only ally is a hidden pilgrim, Painter Crowe -- director of SIGMA Force, an elite command of American scientists and Special Forces operatives -- who is already showing signs of the baffling malady that destroyed the minds of the monks.</p><p>Now it is up to Gray Pierce to save both Painter and Lisa -- and a world in jeopardy -- as SIGMA Force races to expose a century-old plot that threatens to destroy the current world order . . . and alter the destiny of humankind forever.</p><p>Combining the historic scope of <i>The Da Vinci Code</i> with the relentless thrills of today's best action novels, James Rollins's <i>Black Order</i> is a classic adventure -- an ingenious and breathtaking tour de force that explodes with revelations . . . while offering a startling new view of our place in the grand scheme of existence.</p></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3062440231673566849">4.0 stars. Having just finished book three of the Sigma Force series, I can certainly say I am a fan. I love the premise which is basically special forces agents with PhDs in multiple sciences working for a secret arm of DARPA (Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency) hunting down rogue technology and terrorists. Great action, smart, slick plots and a bunch of real "good guy" characters. Certainly the literary equivalent of junk food but it really tastes good. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2049526620" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2049526620" />
    <a title="Shāfiya Mū  (The Djinn Reader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11405894-sh-fiya-m-the-djinn-reader"><img alt="Shāfiya Mū  (The Djinn Reader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598897002p2/11405894.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2049526620?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shāfiya Mū  (The Djinn Reader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shāfiya Mū  (The Djinn Reader)" href="/user/show/11405894-sh-fiya-m-the-djinn-reader">Shāfiya Mū  (The Djinn Reader)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780062017895" href="/book/show/9591472-black-order">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11405894-sh-fiya-m-the-djinn-reader?shelf=fiction-lit">fiction-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2049526620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7883500698441300114">In <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/294042.Black_Order__Sigma_Force___3_' title='Black Order (Sigma Force, #3) by James Rollins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Black Order</a>
</i> written by James Rollins, which is book number three of the <i>Sigma Force</i> series, our group returns to investigate a mysterious plague-like disease that is sweeping it’s way across the villages and temples surrounding Mount Everest. The disease also causes some very intense episodes of psychotic behaviour that cause the infected to murder relentlessly. Meanwhile, in other parts of the world, a powerful piece of Nazi technology is discovered, and one of the world’s wealthiest fam</span>
  <span id="freeText7883500698441300114" style="display:none">In <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/294042.Black_Order__Sigma_Force___3_" title="Black Order (Sigma Force, #3) by James Rollins" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Order</a>
</i> written by James Rollins, which is book number three of the <i>Sigma Force</i> series, our group returns to investigate a mysterious plague-like disease that is sweeping it’s way across the villages and temples surrounding Mount Everest. The disease also causes some very intense episodes of psychotic behaviour that cause the infected to murder relentlessly. Meanwhile, in other parts of the world, a powerful piece of Nazi technology is discovered, and one of the world’s wealthiest families finally make their public appearance, leading to devastating discoveries.<br /><br />My biggest issue with this novel was that it never felt like it was moving forward until the last two-hundred pages. Even then, it was super rushed and abrupt in execution. I felt that the story was starting to run out of pages and needed to immediately change its course of action in regards to character placement and story progression.<br /><br />In the very beginning we get a flashback from World War II era Germany, but this never really plays a big part in the overall story. The Prologue came off as being wholly unnecessary when you look at the bigger picture. I bring this up first and foremost because this chapter sets up the mood and atmosphere for the entire book. Upon reading the Prologue, you end up with these expectations of a jaw-dropping story that will be laced in Nazi technology and crazy ass revelations, but it never arrives.<br /><br />In the first two books of the series, Sigma Force goes from one part of the world to the next hunting down clues that will lead to new information and loot. In <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/294042.Black_Order__Sigma_Force___3_" title="Black Order (Sigma Force, #3) by James Rollins" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Order</a>
</i>, it’s 600-pages of them chasing down material regarding one item and one overarching issue. Normally, I wouldn’t mind such a change in format. When you have a series that spans thirteen books, you have to learn to get creative. But the execution of this narrative was so terrible that it left me wanting so much more knowledge and fresh new action scenes than was given.<br /><br />The device that Sigma Force is hunting is from World War II and all of the data that they uncover in regards to it just adds on to the previous data acquired. It became wholeheartedly repetitive as it continued to blazingly emphasise how the data affects what we already know, and that it’s a dangerous, gargantuan risk to the world. The science is explained to people who are supposed to be elite specialists in very simple, Layman’s terms. Again, normally this wouldn’t bother me too much. But for a third instalment with characters who are capable of comprehending this intellectual level of stuff, it just didn’t fit. You could argue that it was done for the reader, however. It wasn’t written like this in the first two novels, where it would have been more applicable, and it detracts from the reliability of our characters’ wiles.<br /><br />For the first 300-pages to 400-pages, the foundation for the finale is being laid out. That’s more than half of the book’s total length! It should not take 400-pages to build a plot infrastructure, especially if that finale doesn’t need rely on it all. Remember earlier how I mentioned that the last quarter felt very abrupt? When we hit the four-fifty to five hundred mark, one of our characters is magically poofed from one corner of the world to another. There was very little to no context on how he got there. In the process of his travelling, he also learned key information that would help him assist his teammates, with no explanation. Maybe he squeezed it out of the clouds, I don’t know.<br /><br />Lastly, and this probably irked me the most out of everything else, it was agonisingly predictable. The novel followed every trope of the genre that you could think of. Originally, the series had a few tropes here and there, but it always had some element of a twist to it to maintain suspense and avoid monotony. The predictability of <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/294042.Black_Order__Sigma_Force___3_" title="Black Order (Sigma Force, #3) by James Rollins" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Order</a>
</i> severely detracted from any sense of tension that could have existed. I found myself to be utterly bored and unimpressed with the arrival of each trope.<br /><br />The only redeeming quality of <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/294042.Black_Order__Sigma_Force___3_" title="Black Order (Sigma Force, #3) by James Rollins" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Order</a>
</i> was the lore used to create it. I did find the technology they discovered and the physics behind it to be immensely fascinating. The history and the understanding of how it works and what makes it work is the type of science that I attract to with an unnatural hunger. But I couldn’t appreciate anything beyond that.<br /><br />Also, please note that the book does have strong themes of Nazi sympathising, depending on the context of certain situations and scenarios. I know that this may be harmful for some readers.<br /><br />Overall, I don’t recommend the <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/294042.Black_Order__Sigma_Force___3_" title="Black Order (Sigma Force, #3) by James Rollins" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Order</a>
</i>, but I do believe that its contents may surface later on in the series. I have started reading the fourth instalment, The Judas Strain, which already feels immeasurably better than this narrative. So, if you wish to read the series, you may want to find a summary for this, or go into it fully prepared for what’s to come.<br /><br /><b>2.75 hyenas outta 5!</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>TRIGGER WARNING: Ableist language. Brief racist language, specifically against black people. Nazi sympathisers. Animal abuse.</b>
</blockquote><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7883500698441300114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_41955432" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41955432" />
    <a title="Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1709422-jean"><img alt="Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416431345p2/1709422.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41955432?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean" href="/user/show/1709422-jean">Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1709422-jean?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41955432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6968629997732888448">"The truth is too beautiful to die and too monstrous to set free."<br/><br/>It sounded like a melodramatic statement on the part of a doomed Nazi scientist at first, but when I actually got to the ending of the book... I felt that these words, repeated throughout the second half of the book, were truly appropriate for the conclusion of the book.<br/><br/><i>Black Order</i> felt a little different than Rollins' other books. It seemed a little less frantic, but also a little less coherent; I attribute this to the fact that </span>
  <span id="freeText6968629997732888448" style="display:none">"The truth is too beautiful to die and too monstrous to set free."<br /><br />It sounded like a melodramatic statement on the part of a doomed Nazi scientist at first, but when I actually got to the ending of the book... I felt that these words, repeated throughout the second half of the book, were truly appropriate for the conclusion of the book.<br /><br /><i>Black Order</i> felt a little different than Rollins' other books. It seemed a little less frantic, but also a little less coherent; I attribute this to the fact that it simultaneously runs through multiple storylines and none can each receive the same in-depth treatment that I'm used to in his novels. But this approach brought together a larger cast of old characters and new: Painter is in Nepal, Gray is in Denmark, some new folks are in South Africa, and Monk &amp; Kat are back home in Washington. (At first.) Eventually, all the diverse strands of the plot come together, of course. The bad guys were even flatter than Rollins' usual (maybe that's because this is the first where we're not questioning a mole in Sigma) and the relationships and dialogue again seemed forced.<br /><br />The elements of the story were fairly thought-provoking, however. I am completely uneducated on the ancient topics of Rollins' other books, but I found some elements of <i>Black Order</i> that were familiar to me. With a little poking around on the internet, I was able to separate the fact from fiction myself and was pleased with what I found. Nazi biological experiments and Himmler's fascination with the Occult are historical fact, though they have proven ripe for fictional conspiracy theories (and no one seems to feel too bad about playing around with the reality of their atrocities...) I can't speak for how accurately Rollins explained quantum mechanics, but as usual, I was able to follow it and it seemed to gel with what little I have learned about it. Rollins' exploration on quantum evolution, I've learned, is a real, but very controversial theory. Where Rollins takes that theory is of course, fictional.<br /><br />But I think where he went with the ideas was the best part of the book: imagining what new thoughts in science could mean for humanity, much like you'd find in a good sci-fi novel (not that I'd classify <i>Black Order</i> as sci-fi.) Rollins contrived a truly <i>beautiful</i> conclusion to the mystery. That's why I give this one four stars, despite the fact that I do have complaints about other aspects. I suppose I liked this sort of slant because I love fantasy and I love having my imagination stimulted like this. Rollins let his imagination take the ideas of quantum evolution to an almost religious place, though he also makes it clear that it's a science that's dangerous to mess with. Like Gray's own investigations into the yin &amp; yang, it's beautiful and monstrous at the same time.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6968629997732888448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_314120790" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/314120790" />
    <a title="Jaq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4917922-jaq"><img alt="Jaq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582433815p2/4917922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/314120790?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaq" href="/user/show/4917922-jaq">Jaq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer314120790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10490099018991387589">Curse you James Rollins! You kept me up until nearly two a.m. on a school night because I had to finish this book.<br/><br/>As with any author, Mr. Rollins has a distinctive style of writing, that leads me to know somewhat how the story will unfold. Because of this, I can only read one of his books every couple of months. Here's what I like about Mr. Rollins's books:<br/>1. They fit directly into their genre<br/>2. No One is precious (if you read him, I think you'll understand this a bit more)<br/>3. The characters are </span>
  <span id="freeText10490099018991387589" style="display:none">Curse you James Rollins! You kept me up until nearly two a.m. on a school night because I had to finish this book.<br /><br />As with any author, Mr. Rollins has a distinctive style of writing, that leads me to know somewhat how the story will unfold. Because of this, I can only read one of his books every couple of months. Here's what I like about Mr. Rollins's books:<br />1. They fit directly into their genre<br />2. No One is precious (if you read him, I think you'll understand this a bit more)<br />3. The characters are real people, not 'super' people.<br />4. He does his research. (although he sometimes gets caught up in the "I learned this really cool stuff so I'm going to explain all of it to you" thing. Sometimes it's okay to say "It works because of quantum mechanics" instead of explaining all about quantum mechanics)<br />5. In my opinion, he comes up with original and distinct story lines. I feel that each book can be a stand alone story (the first book I read of his is the seventh book in this series and I understood all of it), but if you read them in order you get a lot of little references and nuances about the characters a lot more. Like inside jokes...<br /><br />This book was great. It integrated the characters well, and I feel that the plot line was quite original. Yes, it has to do a bit with Nazi's, but not in a way I've seen before. It had great potential to become a stereotypical evil Nazi story, but I think that it was kept in check. I also love how he creates a puzzle that you can try to put together for yourself, but if you can't he does bring it all together for you. This may cause some people to feel the books are 'predictable', but I enjoy them quite a bit. This one was no exception.<br /><br />I'd like to finish with another curse: Curse you Chris, you said you have the next one in the series and you don't! Argh!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10490099018991387589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_545231962" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/545231962" />
    <a title="Freda Malone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6938113-freda-malone"><img alt="Freda Malone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418039583p2/6938113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/545231962?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Freda Malone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Freda Malone" href="/user/show/6938113-freda-malone">Freda Malone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6938113-freda-malone?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer545231962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10427153651337154245"><br/><br/><b>Himalayas - Everest Base Camp</b> <br/><br/>Dr. Lisa Cummings has been requested to accompany a senior monk to a nearby monastery. Painter Crowe, Director of DARPA, has been assigned there to investigate a strange affliction. He is then afflicted himself. Dr. Cummings finds a gruesome scene and death. Among the dead, an elder monk has written rune like writing on the wall with his own blood, behaving quite mad before slashing his own throat. As the bombs erupt around the mountain, Lisa Cummings and Painter Cr</span>
  <span id="freeText10427153651337154245" style="display:none"><br /><br /><b>Himalayas - Everest Base Camp</b> <br /><br />Dr. Lisa Cummings has been requested to accompany a senior monk to a nearby monastery. Painter Crowe, Director of DARPA, has been assigned there to investigate a strange affliction. He is then afflicted himself. Dr. Cummings finds a gruesome scene and death. Among the dead, an elder monk has written rune like writing on the wall with his own blood, behaving quite mad before slashing his own throat. As the bombs erupt around the mountain, Lisa Cummings and Painter Crowe’s lives collide and the journey begins. <br /><br /><b>Copenhagen, Denmark (around the same time)</b><br /><br />Commander Grayson Pierce is investigating the bibliophile community in search of a Bible which was once owned by Charles Darwin, father of evolution. He is also surveying principals in connection with several other items up for auction. <br /><br />1) A copy of Gregor Mendel’s 1865 paper on genetics<br />2) Max Planck’s Books on Physics<br />3) Botanist Hugo de Vries’s 1901 diary on plant mutations<br /><br />As he enters a bookstore, he is met with Fiona and the bookstore’s owner. Seems that Gray is not the only one looking for the Bible. The owner decides to trust Gray but the scene quickly changes as assassins try to burn the place down and kill the trio inside. <br /><br /><b>Washington, D.C. (around the same time)</b><br /><br />Monk and Kat also work for DARPA and are instructed to report to duty immediately. Painter has not been heard from and Gray is in trouble. Monk is dispatched to help Gray. <br /><br /><b>Zululand, South Africa - Game Preserve</b><br /><br />A warden of the wildlife game preserve and a Dr. Marcia Fairfield are tracking a rhino in trouble. What they find is beyond comprehension. Sliced and diced, baby rhino pulled out and ripped apart nearby, but it is not the actions of poachers, it is something else. They soon find out and it is more horrifying than the lions or other meat eating vultures in the preserve. Run! <br /><br />Without a doubt, James Rollins has created an action packed novel that keeps you turning the pages. All these locations and their findings have a connection. The Nazis and their experiments, here we go. I am truly amazed by the factual evidence in Rollins books and how he creates fiction around them. This centers around quantum evolution and physics as well as biology and other stuff, not to mention how we ‘became’ and where does god fit in all this. Makes you think. If I were a physicist I might not have liked this book simply because I would have a better understanding of the logistics and obsessively picked it apart. I love the unknown enough to expand my imagination and believe in the story, it is more entertaining that way. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10427153651337154245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6841105744763993614" style="display:none">I read this while I was in the goofy garage during 2014. My delightful friends supported my reading habit, and never once wondered (to me, that is, I have no idea what they said amongst themselves!) why I was asking for Rollins's books.<br /><br />I wanted to read them because they are very entertaining, have enough plot and character development to keep me distracted from being in a public mental health facility, and are intensely visually told stories with deep sci-fi roots and some supernatural almost-Lovecraftian cosmic horror overtones.<br /><br />Here I must say I wanted to read this well past bedtime...got in trouble for reading after lights-out, in fact. The weird kuru-like madness plague was, when I think about it now, a bit strange to be so eager to read in a locked ward....<br /><br />Suited me down to the ground at a time when anything more or less challenging would've been impossible to handle.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7753285-chris?shelf=sigma-force">sigma-force</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer277557848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5983921362662196754">The best Sigma Force novel by far (I've also read no. 5). I always learn so much about Science, Technology and History whenever I read a a Rollins that my head spins! However, the science behind this novel is fascinating, for some they may find it a little hard to grasp, but his characters always explain it so well. The evolutionary bits were amazing, and I find evolution so boring at school - not any more thanks to Physics!<br/><br/>As for the history - there was clearly more to the Nazis than I thought.</span>
  <span id="freeText5983921362662196754" style="display:none">The best Sigma Force novel by far (I've also read no. 5). I always learn so much about Science, Technology and History whenever I read a a Rollins that my head spins! However, the science behind this novel is fascinating, for some they may find it a little hard to grasp, but his characters always explain it so well. The evolutionary bits were amazing, and I find evolution so boring at school - not any more thanks to Physics!<br /><br />As for the history - there was clearly more to the Nazis than I thought. I won's spoil the plot.<br /><br />Probably the best thing about Rollins is that he tells you what's true and what's not and then gives you the books to go and read to learn more - something I am definitely going to do having read this.<br /><br />They just seem to get bigger and better - can't wait for the next one, but I might give my brain a bit of a rest from all the learning!</span>

<div id="review_211500733" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/211500733" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/211500733?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780061120725" href="/book/show/896323.Black_Order">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer211500733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11998272443061874662">Well, I guess I'll never be a Rollins fan. I feel a bit bad about this as I have friends here who really like his work. bear that in mind and realize that my review is subjective...it's how I liked the book.<br/><br/>This one is better (imo) than the other I read by Mr. Rollins (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/294046.The_Judas_Strain__A_Sigma_Force_Novel_' title='The Judas Strain (A Sigma Force Novel) by James Rollins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Judas Strain</a>), but still it lost me. I mean you'd think a book with Nazi scientists, mutant horrors, a chemical/biological threat, daring rescues, harrowing escapes, action...and an/the answer to the ultimate evolutionary ques</span>
  <span id="freeText11998272443061874662" style="display:none">Well, I guess I'll never be a Rollins fan. I feel a bit bad about this as I have friends here who really like his work. bear that in mind and realize that my review is subjective...it's how I liked the book.<br /><br />This one is better (imo) than the other I read by Mr. Rollins (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/294046.The_Judas_Strain__A_Sigma_Force_Novel_" title="The Judas Strain (A Sigma Force Novel) by James Rollins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Judas Strain</a>), but still it lost me. I mean you'd think a book with Nazi scientists, mutant horrors, a chemical/biological threat, daring rescues, harrowing escapes, action...and an/the answer to the ultimate evolutionary questions would hold the interest. <br /><br />And it does/did, sometimes. It caught me at first...we'd dropped back to reliable territory, Nazis escaping with a mystery, a lost secret of some kind and so on. Then we move to an accidentally discovered conspiracy. There's murder, danger...and then we stop for a word from our interpersonal counselor. How will "our" love lives work out...will "I" get the nerve to "pop the question", "what are your intentions" toward that girl? Are "you" just leading her on"? (All these pronouns are of course addressed to our characters from each other to each other.)<br /><br />Sigh.<br /><br />The thing here is I'm sure the very things that "tuned me out" of the story and caused me to say..."get on with it", will be some readers' favorite part. By the time we got to the climactic culmination of the story I was tired of the whole thing, again. I "tuned back in" at the end a bit, but was just as relieved it was over and while I got through it the interpersonal lives of our protagonists had to be nodded to at the end also...of course.<br /><br />The book has some loose historical background which I actually find more interesting than the novel itself (subjects I was already slightly familiar with). As in the last book I read he finishes with a bit of a bibliography and some sources. Some might find this interesting.<br /><br />So, while I have another Rollins book waiting I probably won't read it, at least not now. I have other library books out and waiting (including two Brad Thor novels and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/62291.A_Storm_of_Swords__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___3_" title="A Storm of Swords (A Song of Ice and Fire, #3) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Storm of Swords</a>, a book of not inconsiderable length). To you who are Rollins fans I am sorry I can't rate his books higher, this is my take and my taste. Just not books I enjoy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11998272443061874662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82657160" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82657160" />
    <a title="Meika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/271159-meika"><img alt="Meika" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82657160?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meika" href="/user/show/271159-meika">Meika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780060765378" href="/book/show/1034067.Black_Order">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82657160" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer26928948539134515">I generally compare all secret-society/illuminati/techno-conspiracy novels against Foucault's Pendulum, and against Da Vinci Code. DVC is a 1, FP is a 5. <br/>The characters started out like the usual stock characters... black ops guy, hawt female doc doing research, German engineers with Nazi allegiances... etc ad yawn. But then there was some actual character development! I mean, more than I hoped for from a mass market techno-thriller. They're developed along fairly predictable dimensions (the cha</span>
  <span id="freeText26928948539134515" style="display:none">I generally compare all secret-society/illuminati/techno-conspiracy novels against Foucault's Pendulum, and against Da Vinci Code. DVC is a 1, FP is a 5. <br />The characters started out like the usual stock characters... black ops guy, hawt female doc doing research, German engineers with Nazi allegiances... etc ad yawn. But then there was some actual character development! I mean, more than I hoped for from a mass market techno-thriller. They're developed along fairly predictable dimensions (the characters who get paired up end up caring about each other) but it's not so typical that you have to slog through "and then the Nazi chick seduced the Sigma dude, and the blonde American doc has to save him from her" and you wonder which three James Bond movies the author was trying to <s> plagiarize </s> emulate. <br />I also enjoyed the relative feasibility of the tactical stuff. Like, the helicopters dogfighting in the Himalayas... Rollins actually accounts for aircraft functionality above certain altitudes. And none of this, "jumping out of a helo at 1000 feet and using only your nylon windbreaker as a parachute" crap. No. Also, he knows how NVG work. Nothing a little Wikipedia research couldn't back up but hey... at least he did his Wiki research. Sometimes it's a little far-out. But it IS a mass-market thriller. <br />The plot is pretty simple. And he supports it with a hefty amount of sub-plotting. This is both good and bad. It benefits the story by filling it out, giving the characters more story in which to be multi-dimensional. It also keeps you guessing about how the story is going to unfold (even if you know how it's going to end). It does get a little tedious though, jumping from the Himalayas to Germany, to Washington D.C. to South Africa... and the mini-cliffhangers are a little much (you KNOW they aren't going to die in that sudden catastrophic explosion, or the next one, or the next...). <br />Also, the prosaic interludes of explanation (especially after pieces of dialogue) are distracting. Editors? srsly? <br />But overall, good story. <br /><br />Anyway, I took this along on a long flight, figuring it was the right flavor of literary candy for 6 hours of having your butt crammed into 12 inches of cattle-class seating. Good call. For me anyway. I didn't realize this was in a series - it reads pretty well out of order. </span>
  <a data-text-id="26928948539134515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381767-aaron?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381767-aaron?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381767-aaron?shelf=digital">digital</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381767-aaron?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer913885780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1388825869493680295">Director Painter Crowe and Commander Gray Pierce (along with a few other Sigma Force colleagues) again plunge into action and adventure to save the world from some scary super-science. This time around, the focus is on an intriguing concept which combines quantum mechanics and evolution and the efforts of a secretive dark group with roots in the Nazis - a "Black Order", if you will - to both use it to create a master race and to weaponize it and "devolve" their enemies. Romps through the Himalay</span>
  <span id="freeText1388825869493680295" style="display:none">Director Painter Crowe and Commander Gray Pierce (along with a few other Sigma Force colleagues) again plunge into action and adventure to save the world from some scary super-science. This time around, the focus is on an intriguing concept which combines quantum mechanics and evolution and the efforts of a secretive dark group with roots in the Nazis - a "Black Order", if you will - to both use it to create a master race and to weaponize it and "devolve" their enemies. Romps through the Himalayas, Germany, Denmark, and South Africa filled with shootouts, gas chambers, mysterious runes, and test-tube monsters again make this entry in the series a great diversion for those in the market for something with an Indiana Jones flavor.<br /><br />Is it farfetched? Sure. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Especially the climax, and the final revelation about the genetically "perfect" child. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But it's a well-told tale with some characters that have more than the usual two dimensions. If you can suspend your disbelief, you'll be rewarded. You may even learn something, considering Rollins (as always) appears to have pulled a lot of the theories and history he presents from reality.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1388825869493680295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_33437525" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33437525" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33437525?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/861531-angela">Angela</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33437525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7476488533294881114">Guess it just wasnt my style. The dialog was predictable, trite, and read like a script to a mediocre summer action movie. It didnt give enough credit to the readers, since instead of developing plot and story through understandable events and reactions, the characters stated obvious or unasked-for details to each other. Couldnt get into it. <br/>On the plus side, it talked a little about some ideas about evolution and intelligent design in a somewhat creative way, but even this was washed out by laz</span>
  <span id="freeText7476488533294881114" style="display:none">Guess it just wasnt my style. The dialog was predictable, trite, and read like a script to a mediocre summer action movie. It didnt give enough credit to the readers, since instead of developing plot and story through understandable events and reactions, the characters stated obvious or unasked-for details to each other. Couldnt get into it. <br />On the plus side, it talked a little about some ideas about evolution and intelligent design in a somewhat creative way, but even this was washed out by lazy, fantastical conclusions, and even "magic". <br /><br />Rollins needs to either choose to do something somewhat realistically, or go fantasy, but not both. He didnt make both work in concert with each other in this book.<br /><br />Not recommended. Tossed it in the garbage on the airplane.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7476488533294881114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_40652490" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40652490" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1027031-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442501610p2/1027031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40652490?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/1027031-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780060765378" href="/book/show/1034067.Black_Order">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1027031-angela?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40652490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9821931544975763654">I picked up James Rollins' <i>Black Order</i> on another impulse buy, half-certain that it was going to suck after I'd gotten burned on my last attempt to impulse-buy a thriller. This time around I didn't get a spectacular read, but it turned out to be not half-bad. I did have the disadvantage of coming in partway into a series, which meant several character relationships had been established before the start of this particular story... but it didn't hinder the telling of this one too much.<br/><br/>Turns out th</span>
  <span id="freeText9821931544975763654" style="display:none">I picked up James Rollins' <i>Black Order</i> on another impulse buy, half-certain that it was going to suck after I'd gotten burned on my last attempt to impulse-buy a thriller. This time around I didn't get a spectacular read, but it turned out to be not half-bad. I did have the disadvantage of coming in partway into a series, which meant several character relationships had been established before the start of this particular story... but it didn't hinder the telling of this one too much.<br /><br />Turns out this book is the latest in a series about something called Sigma Force, described by one of the character as "scientists with guns". That in and of itself kind of set the tone for the whole thing with me: i.e., something that's kind of fun and is not to be taken too seriously. Kind of like <i>Voyage to the Bottom of the Sea</i>, in fact. And hell, this story even had Nazis, giant mutated monsters, and a core cast of characters traveling around to exotic locations all over the world. All in all, it did rather read like one of the better <i>Voyage to the Bottom of the Sea</i> plots, even if its attempt to fuse the concepts of evolution and intelligent design into something it called "quantum evolution" was pretty silly. It did at least do it in an entertaining fashion. Two and a half stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9821931544975763654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3611801366774595355">This was a really unputdownable read, which I had to put down on several occasions just to savour the suspense, and to relish the last dash to run through the final third of the book (I’m afraid that, like the nasties of these books, I have also started enjoying the “hunt”). I would like to describe this one as not only a great book with characters that would compel the reader to return to the ‘Sigma Force’, but also as a thriller that deals with enough scientific theories to force even class-bu</span>
  <span id="freeText3611801366774595355" style="display:none">This was a really unputdownable read, which I had to put down on several occasions just to savour the suspense, and to relish the last dash to run through the final third of the book (I’m afraid that, like the nasties of these books, I have also started enjoying the “hunt”). I would like to describe this one as not only a great book with characters that would compel the reader to return to the ‘Sigma Force’, but also as a thriller that deals with enough scientific theories to force even class-bunkers like us to re-read some of the texts that had been surrendered to the vagaries of time decades ago. Highly Recommended.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687834-eadie?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687834-eadie?shelf=audio-2018">audio-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2381590725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3882287202978590424">It was great to be back with the Sigma Force again. Gray Pierce in is Copenhagen with a suspicious bookstore fire. He is involved is a terrifying mystery surrounding horrific experiments performed in a now-abandoned laboratory in the mountains in Poland. Painter Crowe and Lisa Cummings are in a remote monastery in the mountains of Nepal where Buddhist monks are turning to cannibalism and torture. The Sigma team start to piece together and come to the conclusion about the Nazis' experiments that </span>
  <span id="freeText3882287202978590424" style="display:none">It was great to be back with the Sigma Force again. Gray Pierce in is Copenhagen with a suspicious bookstore fire. He is involved is a terrifying mystery surrounding horrific experiments performed in a now-abandoned laboratory in the mountains in Poland. Painter Crowe and Lisa Cummings are in a remote monastery in the mountains of Nepal where Buddhist monks are turning to cannibalism and torture. The Sigma team start to piece together and come to the conclusion about the Nazis' experiments that were going on during the war dealing with evolution and the origin of life. They must now save the world from a new order that is on the rise.<br /><br />I liked all the information that we were given in regards to what the Nazis were up to. Never heard or read anything as in depth as this book. James Rollins has given us a mixture of science and heart pumping action and adventure where in some place you need to suspend your beliefs. All in all, it is a riveting edge-of-your seat read that will keep the pages turning quickly. I now look forward to the next Sigma Force book and I would highly recommend this book to those who love scientific adventure reads.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3882287202978590424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer453762123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7001485488942591476">Sort of a James Bond meets Angels and Demons thing here... But faster paced than either of them.<br/><br/>Some of this is straight from James Bond... We have the bad guys in their mountain fortress, including its own internal railway system. We have the hero at an auction for a rare item, although in this case it's his companion who, with nimble fingers, swaps the real item for a fake and tells the hero that if he'd won it "I would've said it was a fake".<br/><br/>Another scene right out of Star Wars. Our captured </span>
  <span id="freeText7001485488942591476" style="display:none">Sort of a James Bond meets Angels and Demons thing here... But faster paced than either of them.<br /><br />Some of this is straight from James Bond... We have the bad guys in their mountain fortress, including its own internal railway system. We have the hero at an auction for a rare item, although in this case it's his companion who, with nimble fingers, swaps the real item for a fake and tells the hero that if he'd won it "I would've said it was a fake".<br /><br />Another scene right out of Star Wars. Our captured hero tries to save his friends' lives by telling the supreme evil bad guy the secret information and the bad guy says "I believe you're right. Now kill his friends." A little later there's "Open the blast shield!" too...<br /><br />And we've got the fantastic, futuristic energy source that can be used for many things, including supplying power, genetic manipulation and mass destruction, depending who controls it. And by the end this gets combined with prayer and mysticism... Whoah!<br /><br />And why, oh why, are the heros so dumb? In Rollins' Sigma Force, they're all ex-special forces operators who got recruited by DARPA for it's super elite team, sent back to college to earn multiple PhD's each as part of their training. Why do they keep making stupid mistakes? How can they keep letting a fifteen year old runaway girl outsmart them, steal their wallets and continually make them do what she wants?<br /><br />This book follows after "Map of Bones" and makes some references to events in that story, Gray's relationship with Rachel, Monk's loss of a hand, Monk and Kat's relationship (bearing fruit in this book). Mostly it could probably be read without having read "Map of Bones" which I read without having read any previous Sigma Force novels.<br /><br />Overall, it's fast, action-packed and entertaining, as long as you can suspend disbelief in a few places and don't expect anything deep...<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7001485488942591476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13859565549766326773" style="display:none">Gray and Monk are in Copenhagen working on a minor US DARPA mission involving an international auction where very important WWII German scientist documents are being scooped up by one group. Something goes wrong and Gray and Monk are basically chased out of town and following a lead end up in Germany.<br /><br />Painter and Lisa are in Nepal. Painter is the head of SIGMA's DARPA group and is investigating strange happenings and mysterious deaths. Lisa is a doctor who basically gets kidnapped off Mt Everest while hiking to help figure out an epidemic at a local monestary. They get kidnapped and are brought to a separate location in Germany.<br /><br />Meanwhile in South Africa, a mutant animal has attacked a UK MI5 agent. After this, all hell breaks loose and everyone converges on South Africa.<br /><br />This book was amazing! Very involved -- quantum physics, evolution, nazis, the Ayran race -- multiple plot and many good guys and even more bad guys spanning the globe. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zxFC1mnqdmwmT0VPalaysH/GDkqBX/uvZM6mhU/gfKbo+SJpvaLFf+tcENQ0k7knC907ITZuXlDL+2L33zzKnw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0VvwhEGzhI65ZIvaH5SVXHcuQ8U7dWAgP0hkLGhhmnf2s5A7lfs3nXR33kFBUZ7LAzV2roxExd+QfaBe+L0sTg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10089107643353246905">James Rollins is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of international thrillers. His writing has been translated into more than forty languages and has sold more than 20 million books. The New York Times says, “Rollins is what you might wind up with if you tossed Michael Crichton and Dan Brown into a particle accelerator together.” NPR calls his work, “Adventurous and enormously engrossing.” </span>
  <span id="freeText10089107643353246905" style="display:none">James Rollins is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of international thrillers. His writing has been translated into more than forty languages and has sold more than 20 million books. The New York Times says, “Rollins is what you might wind up with if you tossed Michael Crichton and Dan Brown into a particle accelerator together.” NPR calls his work, “Adventurous and enormously engrossing.” Rollins unveils unseen worlds, scientific breakthroughs, and historical secrets matched with stunning suspense. As a veterinarian, he had a practice in Sacramento for over a decade and still volunteers at local shelters. Nowadays, Rollins shares his home up in the Sierra Nevada Mountains with his two golden retrievers, Echo and Duncan. He also enjoys scuba diving, spelunking, kayaking, and hiking. Of course, he loves to travel and experience new places around the world, which often inspire his next globe-trotting adventure.</span>
